Let  
GT(v,x) = \(-0.0441723168923102\,v^3\)  \(- 0.333481093540657\,v(1-v^2)\)  \(- 1.24947480809752\,v\)  \(- 0.624737404048761\log(|v|+1)\)  \(- 3.58220621454007\,x\,(0.0479281989045915|v|^{1/3}+1)\).

First simplify the polynomial-in-\(v\) part:
- \(-0.333481093540657\,v(1-v^2)= -0.333481093540657\,v + 0.333481093540657\,v^3\).
So total \(v^3\) coefficient is \(0.333481093540657-0.0441723168923102 = 0.2893087766483468\).
Total \(v\) coefficient is \(-0.333481093540657-1.24947480809752 = -1.582955901638177\).

Also the \(x\)-dependent part is
\[
-3.58220621454007\,x \;-\; (3.58220621454007\cdot 0.0479281989045915)\,x\,|v|^{1/3},
\]
so it contains **both** an \(x\) term and an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term, plus a \(\log(|v|+1)\) term, plus \(v\) and \(v^3\).

Thus any matching candidate (possibly under a domain restriction like \(v\ge 0\) so \(|v|=v\)) must be able to represent simultaneously:
- a \(\log(|v|+1)\) term with fixed “+1 inside log” structure,
- an \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term (fractional power \(1/3\)),
- an \(x\) term,
- \(v\) and \(v^3\) terms.

Now check candidates.

1) Polynomial in \(x\) + \(v\), \(v^3\), and \(\exp(c3 x)|v|\). No \(\log\), no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Cannot match.

2) Rational terms with denominator \(c1+|v|\) and one \(v\exp(c8|v|)\) term. No \(\log(|v|+1)\) and no fractional power \( |v|^{1/3}\) multiplied by \(x\). Cannot match.

3) Has \(\exp(c6 x)\log(c7|v|+1)\) which couples \(x\) and \(\log\). GT has \(\log(|v|+1)\) **independent of \(x\)**. You could set \(c5=0\) to remove the log entirely, but GT needs it. If you try \(c6=0\), then term becomes constant\(\cdot \log(c7|v|+1)\), but still multiplied by \(c5\) only (ok), yet GT also needs \(x|v|^{1/3}\) which this candidate cannot produce. Cannot match.

4) Has \(\exp(c7 x)\log(\cdot)\) again couples \(x\) with log; no \(x|v|^{1/3}\). Cannot match.

5) Piecewise Max terms and \(v^3\), linear \(x\), but no \(\log\) and no fractional power. Cannot match.

You cannot choose constants to make \(\log(a\log(b|v|+1)+1)\) equal \(\log(|v|+1)\) for all \(v\) on any continuous domain (it would require \(a\log(b|v|+1)+1 = |v|+1\), impossible as LHS is logarithmic in \(|v|\)). I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare each candidate to it.

**GT numerical expression:**
`-0.0441723*v³ - 0.333481*v*(1 - v²) - 1.24947*v - 3.58221*x*(0.047928*|v|^(1/3) + 1) - 0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.0441723*v³`
- `-0.333481*v + 0.333481*v³`
- `-1.24947*v`
- `-3.58221*x*0.047928*|v|^(1/3) - 3.58221*x`
- `-0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

Combining terms:
- **v³**: (-0.0441723 + 0.333481) = 0.289309*v³
- **v**: (-0.333481 - 1.24947) = -1.58295*v
- **x·|v|^(1/3)**: -0.171717*x*|v|^(1/3)
- **x**: -3.58221*x
- **log(|v|+1)**: -0.624737*log(|v|+1)

So GT = **0.289309·v³ - 1.58295·v - 0.171717·x·|v|^(1/3) - 3.58221·x - 0.624737·log(|v|+1)**

The key basis functions are:
1. v³
2. v
3. x·|v|^(1/3)
4. x
5. log(|v|+1)

Now I'll check each candidate for the presence of these basis functions (especially x·|v|^(1/3) and log(|v|+1), which are the most distinctive).

**Key observations:**
- Most candidates use polynomial terms (x³, x², etc.) instead of x·|v|^(1/3) — these cannot match.
- The GT has NO x², x³ terms. Candidates with x³, x² would need those coefficients to be zero, but then they'd lose the x·|v|^(1/3) term.
- The GT requires log(|v|+1) — very few candidates have this.
- The GT requires x·|v|^(1/3) — almost no candidates have this.

Let me check candidates that might have the right structure:

**Candidates with log terms:** 3, 4, 22, 24, 26, 46

**Candidate 3:** Has x³, x², v·x², x, exp(c6·x)·log(c7·|v|+1), v, v·|v|. The exp(c6·x)·log(...) can become log(...) if c6=0. Then we get log(c7·|v|+1). But we still need x·|v|^(1/3), which isn't available. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 22:** c0·x·exp(c1·x) + c2·v·|v| + c3·log(c4·log(c5·|v|+1)+1) + c6·v·exp(c7·x). Has log(log(...)+1), not log(|v|+1). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 26:** x³, x², v·x², x, exp(c6·x)·log(c7·|v|+1), v. Setting c6=0 gives log. But no x·|v|^(1/3). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 46:** Similar to 22 with log(log(...)). NO MATCH.
